<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Sustainable Development Goals</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">set of 17 global development goals defined by the United Nations for the year 2030</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:271px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UN_SDG_Logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/UN_SDG_Logo.png/269px-UN_SDG_Logo.png" width="269" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/UN_SDG_Logo.png/404px-UN_SDG_Logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6f/UN_SDG_Logo.png 2x" data-file-width="483" data-file-height="465" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UN_SDG_Logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Sustainable Development Goals are a UN Initiative.</div></div></div><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"SDG" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/SDG_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="SDG (disambiguation)">SDG (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p><b>Sustainable Development Goals</b> (<b>SDGs</b>) (or <b>Global Goals for Sustainable Development</b>) are a collection of 17 global goals set by the United Nations General Assembly. The SDGs are part of Resolution 70/1 of the United Nations General Assembly<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>: "Transforming our World: the 2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development." That has been shortened to "<b>2030 Agenda</b>."<sup id="cite_ref-:3_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The goals are broad and interdependent, yet each has a separate list of targets to achieve. Achieving all 169 targets would signal accomplishing all 17 goals. The SDGs cover social and economic development issues including <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">hunger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water,</a> <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_protection" title="Environmental protection">environment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Paragraph 54 of <a href="/wiki/The_United_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="The United Nations">the United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/UNGA" class="mw-redirect" title="UNGA">General Assembly</a> Resolution A/RES/70/1 of 25 September 2015 contains the goals and targets.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The UN-led process involved its 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">Member States</a> and global <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil society</a>. The resolution is a broad intergovernmental agreement that acts as the <a href="/wiki/Post-2015_Development_Agenda" title="Post-2015 Development Agenda">Post-2015 Development Agenda</a>. The SDGs build on the principles agreed upon in Resolution A/RES/66/288, entitled "The Future We Want".<sup id="cite_ref-United_Nations_Official_Document_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Nations_Official_Document-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> This was a non-binding document released as a result of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Sustainable_Development" title="United Nations Conference on Sustainable Development">Rio+20 Conference</a> held in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-United_Nations_Official_Document_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Nations_Official_Document-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
Implementation as of 2016 is described as "Localizing the SDGs" to highlight the role of local institutions and local actors.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Regional efforts included agreements like the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_21" title="Baltic 21">Baltic 2030 Action Plan</a><sup id="cite_ref-:10_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>. Some remain pessimistic about the potential for achieving the SDGs, especially because of estimates of the cost of achieving all 17.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>  However, progress had been reported by 2018. For example, fewer African children under the age of 5 are suffering from <a href="/wiki/Stunted_growth" title="Stunted growth">stunting</a> and wasting. However, the same study concluded that it is unlikely there will be an end to <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-:11_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>   </p><div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#Criticisms"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Criticisms</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Post-2015_Development_Agenda" title="Post-2015 Development Agenda">Post-2015 Development Agenda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sustainable_Development_Goals_(Lima,_Peru)_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sustainable_Development_Goals_%28Lima%2C_Peru%29_1.jpg/240px-Sustainable_Development_Goals_%28Lima%2C_Peru%29_1.jpg" width="240" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sustainable_Development_Goals_%28Lima%2C_Peru%29_1.jpg/360px-Sustainable_Development_Goals_%28Lima%2C_Peru%29_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sustainable_Development_Goals_%28Lima%2C_Peru%29_1.jpg/480px-Sustainable_Development_Goals_%28Lima%2C_Peru%29_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1356" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sustainable_Development_Goals_(Lima,_Peru)_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Young people holding SDG banners in Lima, Peru.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">United Nations Secretary-General</a> from 2007 to 2016, has stated that: "We don’t have plan B because there is no planet B!."<sup id="cite_ref-UN1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> This thought has guided the development of the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs).
</p><p>Negotiations on the <a href="/wiki/Post-2015_Development_Agenda" title="Post-2015 Development Agenda">Post-2015 Development Agenda</a> began in January 2015 and ended in August 2015. A final document was adopted at the UN Sustainable Development Summit in September 2015 in New York City, USA.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 September 2015, the 193 countries of the UN General Assembly adopted the 2030 Development Agenda titled "Transforming our world: the 2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development".<sup id="cite_ref-:3_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> This agenda has 92 paragraphs. Paragraph 51 outlines the 17 Sustainable Development Goals and the associated 169 targets.
</p><p>UN agencies which are part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Group" title="United Nations Development Group">United Nations Development Group</a> decided to support an independent campaign to communicate the new SDGs to a wider audience. This campaign, "Project Everyone," had the support of corporate institutions and other international organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Using the text drafted by diplomats at the UN level, a team of communication specialists developed icons for every goal<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>. They also shortened the title "The 17 Sustainable Development Goals" to "<a href="/wiki/Global_Goals" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Goals">Global Goals</a>/17#GlobalGoals," then ran workshops and conferences to communicate the Global Goals to a global audience.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Comparison_with_Millennium_Development_Goals_.28MDGs.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparison_with_Millennium_Development_Goals_(MDGs)">Comparison with Millennium Development Goals (MDGs)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Comparison with Millennium Development Goals (MDGs)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The SDGs were developed to succeed the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a> (MDGs) which ended in 2015. The gaps and shortcomings of MDG Goal 8 (To develop a global partnership for development) led to identifying a problematic "donor-recipient" relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-post-2015_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-2015-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Instead, the new SDGs favor collective action by all countries.<sup id="cite_ref-post-2015_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-2015-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A commentary in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> in 2015 argued that 169 targets for the SDGs is too many, describing them as "sprawling, misconceived" and "a mess" compared to the eight MDGs used previously.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The MDGs were about development while the SDGs are about sustainable development. Finally, the MDGs used a  sole approach to problems, while the SDGs take into account the inter-connectedness of all the problems.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Whilst the MDGs were strongly criticized by many NGOs as only dealing with the problems, the SDGs deal with the causes of the problems.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_17_goals">The 17 goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The 17 goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are 169 targets for the 17 goals. Each target has between 1 and 3 indicators used to measure progress toward reaching the targets. In total, there are 304 indicators that will measure compliance.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> has been asked to provide easy to understand lists of targets and facts and figures for each of the 17 SDGs.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The 17 goals listed below as sub-headings use the 2-to-4 word phrases that identify each goal. Directly below each goal, in quotation marks, is the exact wording of the goal in one sentence. The paragraphs that follow present some information about a few targets and indicators related to each goal.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:789px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sustainable_Development_Goals_chart.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/Sustainable_Development_Goals_chart.svg/787px-Sustainable_Development_Goals_chart.svg.png" width="787" height="608" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/Sustainable_Development_Goals_chart.svg/1181px-Sustainable_Development_Goals_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/Sustainable_Development_Goals_chart.svg/1574px-Sustainable_Development_Goals_chart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="278" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sustainable_Development_Goals_chart.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A diagram listing the 17 Sustainable Development Goals</div></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_1:_No_poverty">Goal 1: No poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Goal 1: No poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22End_poverty_in_all_its_forms_everywhere..22.5B20.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;End_poverty_in_all_its_forms_everywhere.&quot;[20]">"End poverty in all its forms everywhere."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: &quot;End poverty in all its forms everywhere.&quot;[20]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Extreme_poverty" title="Extreme poverty">Extreme poverty</a> has been cut by more than half since 1990. Still, more than 1 in 5 people live on less than the target figure of US$1.25 per day. That target may not be adequate for human <a href="/wiki/Subsistence" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsistence">subsistence</a>, however. Some suggest it may be necessary to raise the <a href="/wiki/Poverty_threshold" title="Poverty threshold">poverty line</a> figure to as high as $5 per day.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Poverty is more than the lack of income or resources. People live in poverty if they lack basic services such as healthcare, security, and education. They also experience hunger, social <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a>, and exclusion from decision-making processes.
</p><p>Children make up the majority – more than half – of those living in extreme poverty. In 2013, an estimated 385 million children lived on less than US$1.90 per day. <sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Still, these figures are unreliable due to huge gaps in data on the status of children worldwide. On average, 97 percent of countries have insufficient data to determine the state of impoverished children and make projections towards SDG Goal 1, and 63 percent of countries have no data on child poverty at all. <sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gender_inequality" title="Gender inequality">Gender inequality</a> plays a large role in perpetuating poverty and its risks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Women face potentially life-threatening risks from early <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy" title="Pregnancy">pregnancy</a> and frequent pregnancies. This can result in lost hope for an education and for a better income.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Poverty affects age groups differently, with the most devastating effects experienced by children. It affects their education, health, nutrition, and security, impacting emotional and spiritual development.
</p><p>Achieving Goal 1 is hampered by growing inequality, increasingly <a href="/wiki/Fragile_state" title="Fragile state">fragile statehood</a>, and the impacts of <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-D+C/E+Z_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D+C/E+Z-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_2:_Zero_hunger">Goal 2: Zero hunger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Goal 2: Zero hunger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22End_hunger.2C_achieve_food_security_and_improved_nutrition.2C_and_promote_sustainable_agriculture.22..5B25.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;End_hunger,_achieve_food_security_and_improved_nutrition,_and_promote_sustainable_agriculture&quot;.[25]">"<a href="/wiki/Hunger#Global_initiatives_to_end_hunger" title="Hunger">End hunger</a>, achieve <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a> and improved nutrition, and promote <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_agriculture" title="Sustainable agriculture">sustainable agriculture</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: &quot;End hunger, achieve food security and improved nutrition, and promote sustainable agriculture&quot;.[25]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Goal 2 states that by 2030 we should end hunger and all forms of malnutrition. This would be accomplished by doubling agricultural productivity and incomes of small-scale food producers (especially women and indigenous peoples), by ensuring sustainable food production systems, and by progressively improving land and soil quality. Agriculture is the single largest employer in the world, providing livelihoods for 40% of the global population. It is the largest source of income for poor rural households. Women make up about 43% of the agricultural labor force in <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>, and over 50% in parts of Asia and Africa. However, women own only 20% of the land.
</p><p>Other targets deal with maintaining genetic diversity of seeds, increasing access to land, preventing trade restriction and distortions in world agricultural markets to limit extreme food price volatility, eliminating waste with help from the International Food Waste Coalition, and ending malnutrition and undernutrition of children.
</p><p>Globally, 1 in 9 people are undernourished, the vast majority of whom live in developing countries. Undernutrition causes wasting or severe wasting of 52 million children worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and contributes to nearly half (45%) of deaths in children under five – 3.1 million children per year.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Chronic malnutrition, which affects an estimated 155 million children worldwide, also stunts children's brain and physical development and puts them at further risk of death, disease, and lack of success as adults. <sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017, only 26 of 202 UN member countries are on track to meet the SDG target to eliminate undernourishment and malnourishment, while 20 percent have made no progress at all and nearly 70 percent have no or insufficient data to determine their progress. <sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A report by the <a href="/wiki/International_Food_Policy_Research_Institute" title="International Food Policy Research Institute">International Food Policy Research Institute</a> (IFPRI) of 2013 stated that the emphasis of the SDGs should not be on ending poverty by 2030, but on eliminating hunger and under-nutrition by 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-IFPRI2013_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFPRI2013-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The assertion is based on an analysis of experiences in China, Vietnam, Brazil, and Thailand. Three pathways to achieve this were identified: 1) agriculture-led; 2) social protection- and nutrition- intervention-led; or 3) a combination of both of these approaches.<sup id="cite_ref-IFPRI2013_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFPRI2013-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_3:_Good_health_and_well-being_for_people">Goal 3: Good health and well-being for people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Goal 3: Good health and well-being for people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Ensure_healthy_lives_and_promote_well-being_for_all_at_all_ages..22.5B29.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Ensure_healthy_lives_and_promote_well-being_for_all_at_all_ages.&quot;[29]">"Ensure healthy lives and promote well-being for all at all ages."<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: &quot;Ensure healthy lives and promote well-being for all at all ages.&quot;[29]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Significant strides have been made in increasing life expectancy and reducing some of the common killers associated with <a href="/wiki/Child_mortality" title="Child mortality">child</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maternal_death" title="Maternal death">maternal mortality</a>. Between 2000 and 2016, the worldwide under-five mortality rate decreased by 47 percent (from 78 deaths per 1,000 live births to 41 deaths per 1,000 live births).<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Still, the number of children dying under age five is extremely high: 5.6 million in 2016 alone.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Newborns account for a growing number of these deaths, and poorer children are at the greatest risk of under-5 mortality due to a number of factors.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> SDG Goal 3 aims to reduce under-five mortality to at least as low as 25 per 1,000 live births. But if current trends continue, more than 60 countries will miss the SDG neonatal mortality target for 2030. About half of these countries would not reach the target even by 2050. <sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Goal 3 also aims to reduce maternal mortality to less than 70 deaths per 100,000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-who.int_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Though the maternal mortality ratio declined by 37 percent between 2000 and 2015, there were approximately 303,000 maternal deaths worldwide in 2015, most from preventable causes.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, maternal health conditions were also the leading cause of death among girls aged 15-19. <sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Data for girls of greatest concern – those aged between 10-14 - is currently unavailable. Key strategies for meeting SDG Goal 3 will be to reduce adolescent pregnancy (which is strongly linked to gender equality), provide better data for all women and girls, and achieve universal coverage of skilled birth attendants.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly, progress has been made on increasing access to clean water and sanitation and on reducing <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" title="Poliomyelitis">polio</a>, and the spread of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>.  From 2000-2016, new HIV infections declined by 66 percent for children under 15 and by 45 percent among adolescents aged 15-19.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> However, current trends mean that 1 out of 4 countries still won't meet the SDG target to end AIDS among children under 5, and 3 out of 4 will not meet the target to end AIDS among adolescents.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>  Additionally, only half of women in developing countries have received the health care they need, and the need for <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> is increasing exponentially as the population grows. While needs are being addressed gradually, more than 225 million women have an unmet need for <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">contraception</a>.
</p><p>Goal 3 aims to achieve universal health coverage, including access to essential medicines and vaccines.<sup id="cite_ref-who.int_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> It proposes to end the preventable death of newborns and children under 5 and to end epidemics such as AIDS, tuberculosis, malaria, and water-borne diseases, for example.<sup id="cite_ref-who.int_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> 2016 rates for the third dose of the pertussis vaccine (DTP3) and the first dose of the measles vaccine (MCV1) reached 86 percent and 85 percent, respectively. Yet about 20 million children did not receive DTP3 and about 21 million did not receive MCV1. <sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Around 2 in 5 countries will need to accelerate progress in order to reach SDG targets for immunization.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Attention to health and well-being also includes targets related to the prevention and treatment of <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">substance abuse</a>, deaths and injuries from <a href="/wiki/Traffic_collision" title="Traffic collision">traffic accidents</a> and from hazardous chemicals and air, <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water</a> and soil pollution and contamination.<sup id="cite_ref-who.int_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_4:_Quality_education">Goal 4: Quality education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Goal 4: Quality education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Ensure_inclusive_and_equitable_quality_education_and_promote_lifelong_learning_opportunities_for_all..22.5B31.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Ensure_inclusive_and_equitable_quality_education_and_promote_lifelong_learning_opportunities_for_all.&quot;[31]">"Ensure <a href="/wiki/Inclusion_(education)" title="Inclusion (education)">inclusive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Educational_equity" title="Educational equity">equitable</a> quality education and promote <a href="/wiki/Lifelong_learning" title="Lifelong learning">lifelong learning</a> opportunities for all."<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: &quot;Ensure inclusive and equitable quality education and promote lifelong learning opportunities for all.&quot;[31]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Major progress has been made in access to education, specifically at the <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary school</a> level, for both boys and girls. Still, at least 22 million children in 43 countries will miss out on pre-primary education unless the rate of progress doubles.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Access does not always mean quality of education or completion of primary school. 103 million youth worldwide still lack basic literacy skills, and more than 60 percent of those are women.  In one out of four countries, more than half of children failed to meet minimum math proficiency standards at the end of primary school, and at the lower secondary level, the rate was 1 in 3 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Target 1 of Goal 4 is to ensure that, by 2030, all girls and boys complete free, equitable, and quality primary and secondary education.
</p><p>Additionally, progress is difficult to track: 75 percent of countries have no or insufficient data to track progress towards SDG Goal 4 targets for learning outcomes (target 1), early childhood education (target 2), and effective learning environments.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Data on learning outcomes and pre-primary school are particularly scarce; 70 percent and 40 percent of countries lack adequate data for these targets, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> This makes it hard to analyze and identify the children at greatest risk of being left behind.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_5:_Gender_equality">Goal 5: Gender equality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Goal 5: Gender equality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Achieve_gender_equality_and_empower_all_women_and_girls..22.5B32.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Achieve_gender_equality_and_empower_all_women_and_girls.&quot;[32]">"Achieve <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empowerment" title="Empowerment">empower</a> all women and girls."<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: &quot;Achieve gender equality and empower all women and girls.&quot;[32]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to the UN, "gender equality is not only a fundamental human right, but a necessary foundation for a peaceful, prosperous and sustainable world."<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Providing women and girls with equal access to education, health care, decent work, and representation in political and economic decision-making processes will nurture sustainable economies and benefit societies and humanity at large. A record 143 countries guaranteed equality between men and women in their constitutions as of 2014. However, another 52 had not taken this step. In many nations, gender discrimination is still woven into the fabric of legal systems and social norms. Even though SDG5 is a stand-alone goal, other SDGs can only be achieved if the needs of women receive the same attention as the needs of men. Issues unique to women and girls include traditional practices against all women and girls in the public and private spheres, such as female genital mutilation.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Child_marriage" title="Child marriage">Child marriage</a> has declined over the past decades, yet there is no region that is currently on track to eliminate the practice and reach SDG targets by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> If current trends continue, between 2017 and 2030, 150 million girls will be married before they turn 18.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Though child marriages are four times higher among the poorest than the wealthiest in the world, most countries need to accelerate progress among both groups in order to reach the SDG Goal 5 target to eliminate child marriage by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Achieving gender equality will require enforceable legislation that promotes empowerment of all women and girls and requires secondary education for all girls.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The targets call for an end to gender discrimination and for empowering women and girls through technology<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Some have advocated for "listening to girls". The assertion is that the SDGs can deliver transformative change for girls only if girls are consulted. Their priorities and needs must be taken into account. Girls should be viewed not as beneficiaries of change, but as agents of change. Engaging women and girls in the implementation of the SDGs is crucial.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Pensions_%26_Investments_Forum" title="World Pensions &amp; Investments Forum">World Pensions Council (WPC)</a> has insisted on the transformational role <a href="/wiki/Gender_diversity" title="Gender diversity">gender-diverse</a> that boards can play in that regard, predicting that 2018 could be a pivotal year, as “more than ever before, many UK and European Union <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">pension trustees</a> speak enthusiastically about flexing their <a href="/wiki/Fiduciary" title="Fiduciary">fiduciary</a> muscles for the UN’s Sustainable Development Goals, including SDG5, and to achieve gender equality and empower all women and girls.”<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_6:_Clean_water_and_sanitation">Goal 6: Clean water and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Goal 6: Clean water and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:School_toilet_2_-_WASH_in_schools_(Bangladesh)_(38403428742).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/School_toilet_2_-_WASH_in_schools_%28Bangladesh%29_%2838403428742%29.jpg/220px-School_toilet_2_-_WASH_in_schools_%28Bangladesh%29_%2838403428742%29.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/School_toilet_2_-_WASH_in_schools_%28Bangladesh%29_%2838403428742%29.jpg/330px-School_toilet_2_-_WASH_in_schools_%28Bangladesh%29_%2838403428742%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/School_toilet_2_-_WASH_in_schools_%28Bangladesh%29_%2838403428742%29.jpg/440px-School_toilet_2_-_WASH_in_schools_%28Bangladesh%29_%2838403428742%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:School_toilet_2_-_WASH_in_schools_(Bangladesh)_(38403428742).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Example of sanitation for all: School toilet (IPH school and college, Mohakhali, Dhaka, Bangladesh)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pit_latrines_in_Zambia_(3233256285).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Pit_latrines_in_Zambia_%283233256285%29.jpg/220px-Pit_latrines_in_Zambia_%283233256285%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Pit_latrines_in_Zambia_%283233256285%29.jpg/330px-Pit_latrines_in_Zambia_%283233256285%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Pit_latrines_in_Zambia_%283233256285%29.jpg/440px-Pit_latrines_in_Zambia_%283233256285%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pit_latrines_in_Zambia_(3233256285).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Unimproved sanitation example: <a href="/wiki/Pit_latrine" title="Pit latrine">pit latrine</a> without slab in <a href="/wiki/Lusaka" title="Lusaka">Lusaka</a>, Zambia</div></div></div>
<h4><span id=".22Ensure_availability_and_sustainable_management_of_water_and_sanitation_for_all..22.5B38.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Ensure_availability_and_sustainable_management_of_water_and_sanitation_for_all.&quot;[38]">"Ensure availability and sustainable management of water and sanitation for all."<sup id="cite_ref-SDG6_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDG6-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: &quot;Ensure availability and sustainable management of water and sanitation for all.&quot;[38]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_6" title="Sustainable Development Goal 6">Sustainable Development Goal 6</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_6" title="Sustainable Development Goal 6">Sustainable Development Goal Number 6</a> (SDG6) has eight targets and 11 indicators that will be used to monitor progress toward the targets. Most are to be achieved by the year 2030. One is targeted for 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-SDG6_targets_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDG6_targets-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first three targets relate to drinking <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SDG6_targets_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDG6_targets-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Worldwide, 6 out of 10 people lack safely managed sanitation services, and 3 out of 10 lack safely managed water services.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Safe drinking water and hygienic <a href="/wiki/Toilets" class="mw-redirect" title="Toilets">toilets</a> protect people from disease and enable societies to be more productive economically. Attending school and work without disruption is critical to successful education and successful employment. Therefore, toilets in schools and work places are specifically mentioned as a target to measure. "Equitable sanitation" calls for addressing the specific needs of women and girls and those in vulnerable situations, such as the elderly or people with disabilities. Water sources are better preserved if open defecation is ended and sustainable sanitation systems are implemented.
</p><p>Ending <a href="/wiki/Open_defecation" title="Open defecation">open defecation</a> will require provision of toilets and sanitation for 2.6 billion people as well as <a href="/wiki/Behavior_change_(public_health)" title="Behavior change (public health)">behavior change</a> of the users.<sup id="cite_ref-JMP2017_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JMP2017-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> This will require cooperation between governments, civil society, and the private sector.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main indicator for the sanitation target is the "Proportion of population using safely managed sanitation services, including a hand-washing facility with soap and water".<sup id="cite_ref-:12_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> However, as of 2017, two-thirds of countries lacked baseline estimates for SDG indicators on hand washing, safely managed drinking water, and sanitation services.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> From those that were available, the Joint Monitoring Programme (<a href="/wiki/Joint_Monitoring_Programme_for_Water_Supply_and_Sanitation" title="Joint Monitoring Programme for Water Supply and Sanitation">JMP</a>) found that 4.5 billion people currently do not have <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">safely managed sanitation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JMP2017_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JMP2017-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> If we are to meet SDG targets for sanitation by 2030, nearly one-third of countries will need to accelerate progress to end open defecation including Brazil, China, Ethiopia, India, Indonesia, Nigeria, and Pakistan.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Sanitation_Alliance" title="Sustainable Sanitation Alliance">Sustainable Sanitation Alliance</a> (SuSanA) has made it its mission to achieve SDG6.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> SuSanA's position is that the SDGs are highly interdependent. Therefore, the provision of clean water and sanitation for all is a precursor to achieving many of the other SDGs.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_7:_Affordable_and_clean_energy">Goal 7: Affordable and clean energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Goal 7: Affordable and clean energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Ensure_access_to_affordable.2C_reliable.2C_sustainable_and_modern_energy_for_all..22.5B46.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Ensure_access_to_affordable,_reliable,_sustainable_and_modern_energy_for_all.&quot;[46]">"Ensure access to affordable, reliable, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable</a> and modern energy for all."<sup id="cite_ref-:9_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: &quot;Ensure access to affordable, reliable, sustainable and modern energy for all.&quot;[46]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Targets for 2030 include access to affordable and reliable energy while increasing the share of renewable energy in the global energy mix. This would involve improving energy efficiency and enhancing international cooperation to facilitate more open access to clean energy technology and more investment in clean energy infrastructure. Plans call for particular attention to infrastructure support for the <a href="/wiki/Least_Developed_Countries" title="Least Developed Countries">least developed countries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Small_Island_Developing_States" title="Small Island Developing States">small islands</a> and land-locked <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2017, only 57 percent of the global population relies primarily on clean fuels and technology, falling short of the 95 percent target.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_8:_Decent_work_and_economic_growth">Goal 8: Decent work and economic growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Goal 8: Decent work and economic growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Promote_sustained.2C_inclusive_and_sustainable_economic_growth.2C_full_and_productive_employment_and_decent_work_for_all..22.5B47.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Promote_sustained,_inclusive_and_sustainable_economic_growth,_full_and_productive_employment_and_decent_work_for_all.&quot;[47]">"Promote sustained, inclusive and <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable economic growth</a>, full and productive employment and <a href="/wiki/Decent_work" title="Decent work">decent work</a> for all."<sup id="cite_ref-:6_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: &quot;Promote sustained, inclusive and sustainable economic growth, full and productive employment and decent work for all.&quot;[47]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/World_Pensions_%26_Investments_Forum" title="World Pensions &amp; Investments Forum">World Pensions Council (WPC)</a> development economists have argued that the twin considerations of long-term economic growth and infrastructure investment weren’t prioritized enough. Being prioritized as number 8 and number 9 respectively was considered a rather "mediocre ranking and defies common sense<i>"</i><sup id="cite_ref-Analyse_Financière_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Analyse_Financière-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the least developed countries, the economic target is to attain at least a 7 percent annual growth in gross domestic product (GDP). Achieving higher productivity will require diversification and upgraded technology along with innovation, entrepreneurship, and the growth of small- and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs). Some targets are for 2030; others are for 2020. The target for 2020 is to reduce youth unemployment and operationalize a global strategy for youth employment. Implementing the Global Jobs Pact of the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> is also mentioned.
</p><p>By 2030, the target is to establish policies for sustainable tourism that will create jobs. Strengthening domestic financial institutions and increasing Aid for Trade support for developing countries is considered essential to economic development. The Enhanced Integrated Framework for Trade-Related Technical Assistance to Least Developed Countries is mentioned as a method for achieving sustainable economic development.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Goal_9:_Industry.2C_Innovation.2C_and_Infrastructure"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_9:_Industry,_Innovation,_and_Infrastructure">Goal 9: Industry, Innovation, and Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Goal 9: Industry, Innovation, and Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Build_resilient_infrastructure.2C_promote_inclusive_and_sustainable_industrialization.2C_and_foster_innovation.22..5B49.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Build_resilient_infrastructure,_promote_inclusive_and_sustainable_industrialization,_and_foster_innovation&quot;.[49]">"Build resilient infrastructure, promote inclusive and sustainable industrialization, and foster <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: &quot;Build resilient infrastructure, promote inclusive and sustainable industrialization, and foster innovation&quot;.[49]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Resilience_(engineering_and_construction)" title="Resilience (engineering and construction)">Resilience (engineering and construction)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_resilience" title="Urban resilience">Urban resilience</a></div>
<p>Manufacturing is a major source of employment. In 2016, the least developed countries had less "manufacturing value added per capita". The figure for Europe and North America amounted to US$4,621, compared to about $100 in the least developed countries.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The manufacturing of high products contributes 80 percent to total manufacturing output in industrialized economies but barely 10 percent in the least developed countries.
</p><p>Mobile-cellular signal coverage has improved a great deal. In previously "unconnected" areas of the globe, 85 percent of people now live in covered areas. Planet-wide, 95 percent of the population is covered.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_10:_Reducing_inequalities">Goal 10: Reducing inequalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Goal 10: Reducing inequalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Reduce_income_inequality_within_and_among_countries..22.5B51.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Reduce_income_inequality_within_and_among_countries.&quot;[51]">"Reduce income <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">inequality</a> within and among countries."<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: &quot;Reduce income inequality within and among countries.&quot;[51]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>One target is to reduce the cost of exporting goods from least developed countries. "Duty-free treatment" has expanded. As of 2015, 65 percent of products coming from the least developed countries were duty-free, as compared to 41 percent in 2005.
</p><p>The target of 3 percent was established as the cost that international migrant workers would pay to send money home (known as <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a>). However, post offices and money transfer companies currently charge 6 percent of the amount remitted. Worse, commercial banks charge 11 percent. Prepaid cards and mobile money companies charge 2 to 4 percent, but those services were not widely available as of 2017 in typical "remittance corridors."<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_11:_Sustainable_cities_and_communities">Goal 11: Sustainable cities and communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Goal 11: Sustainable cities and communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Make_cities_and_human_settlements_inclusive.2C_safe.2C_resilient.2C_and_sustainable..22.5B53.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Make_cities_and_human_settlements_inclusive,_safe,_resilient,_and_sustainable.&quot;[53]">"Make cities and human settlements inclusive, safe, resilient, and sustainable."<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: &quot;Make cities and human settlements inclusive, safe, resilient, and sustainable.&quot;[53]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The target for 2030 is to ensure access to safe and <a href="/wiki/Affordable_housing" title="Affordable housing">affordable housing</a>. The indicator named to measure progress toward this target is the proportion of urban population living in <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slums</a> or <a href="/wiki/Shanty_town" title="Shanty town">informal settlements</a>. Between 2000 and 2014, the proportion fell from 39 percent to 30 percent. However, the absolute number of people living in slums went from 792 million in 2000 to an estimated 880 million in 2014. Movement from rural to urban areas has accelerated as the population has grown and better housing alternatives are available.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_12:_Responsible_consumption_and_production">Goal 12: Responsible consumption and production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Goal 12: Responsible consumption and production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Ensure_sustainable_consumption_and_production_patterns..22.5B55.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Ensure_sustainable_consumption_and_production_patterns.&quot;[55]">"Ensure <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_consumption" title="Sustainable consumption">sustainable consumption</a> and production patterns."<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: &quot;Ensure sustainable consumption and production patterns.&quot;[55]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_products" title="Sustainable products">Sustainable products</a></div>
<p>The targets of Goal 12 include using <a href="/wiki/Environmentally_friendly" title="Environmentally friendly">eco-friendly</a> production methods and reducing the amount of waste. By 2030, national <a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recycling</a> rates should increase, as measured in tons of material recycled. Further, companies should adopt sustainable practices and publish sustainability reports.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_13:_Climate_action">Goal 13: Climate action</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Goal 13: Climate action">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Take_urgent_action_to_combat_climate_change_and_its_impacts_by_regulating_emissions_and_promoting_developments_in_renewable_energy..22.5B56.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Take_urgent_action_to_combat_climate_change_and_its_impacts_by_regulating_emissions_and_promoting_developments_in_renewable_energy.&quot;[56]">"Take urgent action to combat <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">climate change</a> and its impacts by regulating <a href="/wiki/Emission_of_greenhouse_gases" class="mw-redirect" title="Emission of greenhouse gases">emissions</a> and promoting developments in <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: &quot;Take urgent action to combat climate change and its impacts by regulating emissions and promoting developments in renewable energy.&quot;[56]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The UN discussions and negotiations identified the links between the post-2015 SDG process and the <a href="/wiki/Financing_for_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Financing for Development">Financing for Development</a> process that concluded in Addis Ababa in July 2015 and the <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2015 United Nations Climate Change Conference">COP 21</a> Climate Change conference in Paris in December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2015, a report concluded that only a very ambitious climate deal in Paris in 2015 could enable countries to reach the sustainable development goals and targets.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
The report also states that tackling climate change will only be possible if the SDGs are met. Further, economic development and climate change are inextricably linked, particularly around <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, and energy. The UN encourages the <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> to take initiative in this effort to minimize <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental impact">negative impacts on the environment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This renewed emphasis on climate change mitigation was made possible by the partial <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="China–United States relations">Sino-American</a> convergence that developed in 2015-2016, notably at the UN <a href="/wiki/COP21" class="mw-redirect" title="COP21">COP21</a> summit (Paris) and ensuing <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> conference (Hangzhou).<sup id="cite_ref-Analyse_Financière_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Analyse_Financière-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As one of the regions most vulnerable to the unprecedented effects of climate change, the Asia-Pacific region needs more Public-Private Partnerships (PPPs) to successfully implement its sustainable development initiatives. <sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_14:_Life_below_water">Goal 14: Life below water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Goal 14: Life below water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Conserve_and_sustainably_use_the_oceans.2C_seas_and_marine_resources_for_sustainable_development..22.5B61.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Conserve_and_sustainably_use_the_oceans,_seas_and_marine_resources_for_sustainable_development.&quot;[61]">"Conserve and sustainably use the oceans, seas and marine resources for sustainable development."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: &quot;Conserve and sustainably use the oceans, seas and marine resources for sustainable development.&quot;[61]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">Oceans</a> cover 71 percent of the Earth's surface. They are essential for making the planet livable. <a href="/wiki/Rainwater" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainwater">Rainwater</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">drinking water</a> and climate are all regulated by <a href="/wiki/Ocean_temperature" class="mw-redirect" title="Ocean temperature">ocean temperatures</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ocean_current" title="Ocean current">currents</a>. Over 3 billion people depend on marine life for their livelihood. Oceans absorb 30 percent of all <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> produced by humans.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP2017_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP2017-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed (February 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The oceans contain more than 200,000 identified species, and there might be thousands of species that are yet to be discovered. Oceans are the world's largest sources of protein. However, there has been a 26 percent increase in <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">acidification</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a>. A full 30 percent of <a href="/wiki/Marine_habitat" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine habitat">marine habitats</a> have been destroyed, and 30 percent of the world's <a href="/wiki/Fish_stocks" class="mw-redirect" title="Fish stocks">fish stocks</a> are <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">over-exploited</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP2017_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP2017-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed (February 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Marine_pollution" title="Marine pollution">Marine pollution</a> has reached shocking levels; each minute, 15 tons of plastic are released into the oceans.<sup id="cite_ref-WWF2017_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WWF2017-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed (February 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> 20 percent of all <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> have been destroyed irreversibly, and another 24 percent are in immediate risk of collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-UN2016_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN2016-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed (February 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Approximately 1 million sea birds, 100 000 marine mammals, and an unknown number of fish are harmed or die annually due to marine pollution caused by humans. It has been found that 95 percent of <a href="/wiki/Fulmar" title="Fulmar">fulmars</a> in Norway have plastic parts in their guts.<sup id="cite_ref-WWF2017_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WWF2017-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed (February 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Microplastics" title="Microplastics">Microplastics</a> are another form of marine pollution.
</p><p>Individuals can help the oceans by reducing their <a href="/wiki/Energy_consumption" title="Energy consumption">energy consumption</a> and their use of plastics. Nations can also take action. In Norway, for instance, citizens, working through a web page called finn.no, can earn money for picking up plastic on the beach.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Several countries, including Kenya, have <a href="/wiki/Phase-out_of_lightweight_plastic_bags" title="Phase-out of lightweight plastic bags">banned the use of plastic bags</a> for retail purchases.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Improving the oceans contributes to <a href="/wiki/Poverty_reduction" title="Poverty reduction">poverty reduction</a>, as it gives low-income families a source of income and healthy food. Keeping beaches and ocean water clean in less developed countries can attract tourism, as stated in Goal 8, and reduce poverty by providing more employment.<sup id="cite_ref-UN2016_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN2016-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed (February 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The targets include preventing and reducing marine pollution and acidification, protecting marine and <a href="/wiki/Coastal_ecosystem" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastal ecosystem">coastal ecosystems</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fishing_regulation" class="mw-redirect" title="Fishing regulation">regulating fishing</a>. The targets also call for an increase in scientific knowledge of the oceans.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_15:_Life_on_land">Goal 15: Life on land</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Goal 15: Life on land">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Protect.2C_restore_and_promote_sustainable_use_of_terrestrial_ecosystems.2C_sustainably_manage_forests.2C_combat_desertification.2C_and_halt_and_reverse_land_degradation_and_halt_biodiversity_loss..22.5B69.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Protect,_restore_and_promote_sustainable_use_of_terrestrial_ecosystems,_sustainably_manage_forests,_combat_desertification,_and_halt_and_reverse_land_degradation_and_halt_biodiversity_loss.&quot;[69]">"Protect, restore and promote sustainable use of terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a>, sustainably manage forests, combat <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>, and halt and reverse <a href="/wiki/Land_degradation" title="Land degradation">land degradation</a> and halt <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> loss."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: &quot;Protect, restore and promote sustainable use of terrestrial ecosystems, sustainably manage forests, combat desertification, and halt and reverse land degradation and halt biodiversity loss.&quot;[69]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This goal articulates targets for preserving biodiversity of forest, desert, and mountain eco-systems, as a percentage of total land mass. Achieving a "land degradation-neutral world" can be reached by restoring degraded forests and land lost to drought and flood. Goal 15 calls for more attention to preventing invasion of <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">introduced species</a> and more protection of <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered species</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:13_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Mountain Green Cover Index monitors progress toward target 15.4, which focuses on preserving mountain ecosystems. The index is named as the indicator for target 15.4.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, the Red Index (Red List Index or RLI) will fill the monitoring function for biodiversity goals by documenting the trajectory of endangered species.<sup id="cite_ref-:13_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Animal extinction is a growing problem.
</p>
<h3><span id="Goal_16:_Peace.2C_justice_and_strong_institutions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_16:_Peace,_justice_and_strong_institutions">Goal 16: Peace, justice and strong institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Goal 16: Peace, justice and strong institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Promote_peaceful_and_inclusive_societies_for_sustainable_development.2C_provide_access_to_justice_for_all_and_build_effective.2C_accountable_and_inclusive_institutions_at_all_levels..22.5B72.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Promote_peaceful_and_inclusive_societies_for_sustainable_development,_provide_access_to_justice_for_all_and_build_effective,_accountable_and_inclusive_institutions_at_all_levels.&quot;[72]">"Promote peaceful and inclusive societies for <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>, provide <a href="/wiki/Right_to_fair_trial" class="mw-redirect" title="Right to fair trial">access to justice</a> for all and build effective, accountable and inclusive institutions at all levels."<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: &quot;Promote peaceful and inclusive societies for sustainable development, provide access to justice for all and build effective, accountable and inclusive institutions at all levels.&quot;[72]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Reducing <a href="/wiki/Violent_crime" title="Violent crime">violent crime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sex_trafficking" title="Sex trafficking">sex trafficking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unfree_labour" title="Unfree labour">forced labor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Child_abuse" title="Child abuse">child abuse</a> are clear global goals. The International Community values <a href="/wiki/Peace" title="Peace">peace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Justice" title="Justice">justice</a> and calls for stronger judicial systems that will enforce laws and work toward a more peaceful and just society. By 2017, the UN could report progress on detecting victims of trafficking. More women and girls than men and boys were victimized, yet the share of women and girls has slowly declined (see also <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">violence against women</a>). In 2004, 84 percent of victims were females and by 2014 that number had dropped to 71 percent. Sexual exploitation numbers have declined, but forced labor has increased.
</p><p>One target is to see the end to sex trafficking, forced labor, and all forms of violence against and torture of children. However, reliance on the indicator of "crimes reported" makes monitoring and achieving this goal challenging.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> For instance, 84 percent of countries have no or insufficient data on violent punishment of children.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Of the data available, it is clear that violence against children by their caregivers remains pervasive: Nearly 8 in 10 children aged 1 to 14 are subjected to violent discipline on a regular basis (regardless of income), and no country is on track to eliminate violent discipline by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>SDG 16 also targets universal legal identity and <a href="/wiki/Birth_certificate" title="Birth certificate">birth registration</a>, ensuring the right to a name and nationality, <a href="/wiki/Civil_and_political_rights" title="Civil and political rights">civil rights</a>, recognition before the law, and access to justice and social services. With more than a quarter of children under 5 unregistered worldwide as of 2015, about 1 in 5 countries will need to accelerate progress to achieve universal birth registration by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-SDGChildren2018_26-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDGChildren2018-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal_17:_Partnerships_for_the_goals">Goal 17: Partnerships for the goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Goal 17: Partnerships for the goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
