<h4><span id=".22Strengthen_the_means_of_implementation_and_revitalize_the_global_partnership_for_sustainable_development..E2.80.9C.5B74.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Strengthen_the_means_of_implementation_and_revitalize_the_global_partnership_for_sustainable_development.“[74]">"Strengthen the means of implementation and revitalize the global partnership for <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>.“<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: &quot;Strengthen the means of implementation and revitalize the global partnership for sustainable development.“[74]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Increasing <a href="/wiki/Multilateralism" title="Multilateralism">international cooperation</a> is seen as vital to achieving each of the 16 previous goals. Goal 17 is included to assure that countries and organizations cooperate instead of compete. Developing multi-stakeholder partnerships to share knowledge, expertise, technology, and financial support is seen as critical to overall success of the SDGs. <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership" title="Public–private partnership">Public-private partnerships</a> that involve civil societies are specifically mentioned.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms">Criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Criticisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competing_goals">Competing goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Competing goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Food_vs._fuel" title="Food vs. fuel">Food vs. fuel</a></div>
<p>First, some of the SDGs might be contradictory. For example, seeking high levels of quantitative <a href="/wiki/GDP_growth" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP growth">GDP growth</a> (as opposed to qualitative economic development and the goal of better distribution of the economic product) might undermine <a href="/wiki/Ecological" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecological">ecological</a>, inequality reduction, and sustainability objectives. Similarly, increasing employment and wages can work against reducing the <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_living" title="Cost of living">cost of living</a>.
</p><p>Second, the goal of achieving sustainable human population and lifestyle levels, and the scientific issues of matching ecosystems (and the Earth as a whole) to the number of human beings that they can sustainably support at a certain life-style level, seem neglected and largely unarticulated. Human population levels and reproductive rates are independent variables in trying to reach the SDGs and in aiming at an overall sustainable Earth/Human Community, they need to be scientifically recognized as such.
</p><p>Third, in addition to population and lifestyle issues, three sectors need to come together in order to achieve sustainable development. These are the economic, socio-political, and environmental sectors in their broadest sense.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> This requires the promotion of <a href="/wiki/Multidisciplinary" class="mw-redirect" title="Multidisciplinary">multidisciplinary</a> and transdisciplinary research across different sectors, which can be difficult, particularly when major governments fail to support it.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>. 
</p><p>Fourth, the issues of demilitarization, disarmament, and conversion to peace-based economies also seem neglected, along with the issues of corruption, drugs, robotization of jobs, the need for global citizenship education, the lack of reliable UN and SDG financing, and the current disempowering inability of citizens to participate directly in the global-level decision-making and priority-setting process and to thereby feel the collective togetherness needed for the success of the SDG effort.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Too_many_goals">Too many goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Too many goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A commentary in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> in 2015 argued that 169 targets for the SDGs is too many, describing them as "sprawling, misconceived" and "a mess".<sup id="cite_ref-:5_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The goals are said to ignore local context. All other 16 goals might be contingent on achieving SDG 1, ending poverty, which should have been at the top of a very short list of goals.
</p><p>On the other hand, nearly all stakeholders engaged in negotiations to develop the SDGs agreed that the high number of 17 goals were justified because the agenda they address is all encompassing.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_cost_of_achieving_the_SDGs">High cost of achieving the SDGs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: High cost of achieving the SDGs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>The Economist</i> estimated that alleviating poverty and achieving the other sustainable development goals will require about $2-$3 trillion USD per year for the next 15 years which they called "pure fantasy".<sup id="cite_ref-:5_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Estimates for providing clean water and sanitation for the whole population of all continents have been as high as US$200 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The World Bank cautions that estimates need to be made country by country, and reevaluated frequently over time.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Responses_to_criticisms">Responses to criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Responses to criticisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Other views are more positive. The SDGs were an outcome from a UN conference that was not criticized by any major <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental organization</a> (NGO). Instead, the SDGs received broad support from many NGOs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> 
</p><p>The Rockefeller Foundation asserts that "The key to financing and achieving the SDGs lies in mobilizing a greater share of the $200+ trillion in annual private capital investment flows toward development efforts, and philanthropy has a critical role to play in catalyzing this shift."<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Large-scale funders participating in a Rockefeller Foundation-hosted design thinking workshop (June 2017: Scaling Solutions) were realistic.  They concluded that while there is a moral imperative to achieve the SDGs, failure is inevitable if there aren't drastic changes to how we go about financing large scale change.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Implementation">Implementation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Implementation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:B-1356@PEK_(20180411153702).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/B-1356%40PEK_%2820180411153702%29.jpg/220px-B-1356%40PEK_%2820180411153702%29.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/B-1356%40PEK_%2820180411153702%29.jpg/330px-B-1356%40PEK_%2820180411153702%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/B-1356%40PEK_%2820180411153702%29.jpg/440px-B-1356%40PEK_%2820180411153702%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4465" data-file-height="2834" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:B-1356@PEK_(20180411153702).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787">Boeing 787</a> of <a href="/wiki/XiamenAir" title="XiamenAir">XiamenAir</a> in Sustainable Development Goals <a href="/wiki/Livery" title="Livery">livery</a> in 2018</div></div></div>
<p>Implementation of the SDGs started worldwide in 2016. This process can also be called "Localizing the SDGs". All over the planet, individual people, universities, governments and institutions and organizations of all kinds work on several goals at the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-globalcitizen.org_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalcitizen.org-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In each country, governments must translate the goals into national legislation, develop a plan of action, establish budgets and at the same time be open to and actively search for partners. Poor countries need the support of rich countries and coordination at the international level is crucial.<sup id="cite_ref-D+C_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D+C-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The independent campaign "Project Everyone" has met some resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In addition, several sections of civil society and governments felt the SDGs ignored "<a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a>" even though it was the most important aspect of the agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2018 study in the journal <i>Nature</i> found that while "nearly all African countries demonstrated improvements for children under 5 years old for stunting, wasting, and underweight... much, if not all of the continent will fail to meet the Sustainable Development Goal target—to end malnutrition by 2030."<sup id="cite_ref-:11_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe_and_Russia">Europe and Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Europe and Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baltic nations, via the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Baltic_Sea_States" title="Council of the Baltic Sea States">Council of the Baltic Sea States</a>, have created the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_21" title="Baltic 21">Baltic 2030 Action Plan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:10_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Pensions_%26_Investments_Forum" title="World Pensions &amp; Investments Forum">World Pensions Forum</a> has observed that UK and <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> <a href="/wiki/Pension_fund" title="Pension fund">pension investors</a> have been at the forefront of ESG-driven asset allocation at home and abroad and <a href="/wiki/Early_adopter" title="Early adopter">early adopters</a> of “SDG-centric” investment practices.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> established the <a href="/wiki/NITI_Aayog" title="NITI Aayog">NITI Aayog</a> to attain the sustainable development goals.<sup id="cite_ref-indgoal1_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indgoal1-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In March 2018 Haryana became the first state in India to have its annual budget focused on the attainment of SDG with a 3-year action plan and a 7-year strategy plan to implement sustainable development goals when <a href="/wiki/Captain_Abhimanyu" title="Captain Abhimanyu">Captain Abhimanyu</a>, Finance Minister of <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Haryana" title="Government of Haryana">Government of Haryana</a>, unveiled a <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">₹</a></span>1,151,980 million</span> (US$16&#160;billion or €14&#160;billion) annual 2018-19 budget.<sup id="cite_ref-ungoal1_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ungoal1-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cross-cutting_issues">Cross-cutting issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Cross-cutting issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women_and_gender_equality">Women and gender equality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Women and gender equality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is widespread consensus that progress on all of the SDGs will be stalled if women's empowerment and gender equality is not prioritized holistically – by policy makers as well as private sector executives and board members. <sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Statements from diverse sources, such as the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development</a> (OECD), <a href="/wiki/UN_Women" title="UN Women">UN Women</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Pensions_%26_Investments_Forum" title="World Pensions &amp; Investments Forum">World Pensions Forum</a> have noted that investments in women and girls have positive impacts on economies. National and global development investments often exceed their initial scope.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_sustainable_development">Education and sustainable development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Education and sustainable development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_for_sustainable_development" title="Education for sustainable development">Education for sustainable development</a></div>
<p>Education for sustainable development (ESD) is explicitly recognized in the SDGs as part of Target 4.7 of the SDG on education. UNESCO promotes the <a href="/wiki/Global_citizenship_education" title="Global citizenship education">Global Citizenship Education</a> (GCED) as a complementary approach.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, it is important to emphasize ESD’s importance for all the other 16 SDGs. With its overall aim to develop cross-cutting sustainability competencies in learners, ESD is an essential contribution to all efforts to achieve the SDGs. This would enable individuals to contribute to sustainable development by promoting societal, economic and political change as well as by transforming their own behavior.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Education.2C_gender_and_technology"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Education,_gender_and_technology">Education, gender and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Education, gender and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Massive_open_online_course" title="Massive open online course">Massive open online course</a></div>
<p>Massive open online courses (MOOCs) are free open education offered through online platforms. The (initial) philosophy of MOOCs was to open up quality <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">Higher Education</a> to a wider audience. As such, MOOCs are an important tool to achieve Goal 4 ("Ensure inclusive and equitable quality education and promote lifelong learning opportunities for all").<sup id="cite_ref-:0_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, MOOCs also contribute to Goal 5, in that they are gender neutral and can give women and girls improved access to education.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SDG-driven_investment">SDG-driven investment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: SDG-driven investment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Stewardship" title="Stewardship">Capital stewardship</a> is expected to play a crucial part in the progressive advancement of the SDG agenda: 
</p>
<dl><dd>“No longer ‘<a href="/wiki/Absentee_landlord" title="Absentee landlord">absentee landlords</a>’, <a href="/wiki/Pension_fund" title="Pension fund">pension fund</a> trustees have started to exercise more forcefully their <a href="/wiki/Governance" title="Governance">governance</a> prerogatives across the boardrooms of Britain, Benelux and America: coming together through the establishment of engaged pressure groups [...] to shift the [whole economic] system towards sustainable investment”<sup id="cite_ref-Revue_Analyse_Financiere_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Revue_Analyse_Financiere-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> by using the SDG framework across all <a href="/wiki/Asset_class" class="mw-redirect" title="Asset class">asset classes</a> <sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Post-2015_Development_Agenda" title="Post-2015 Development Agenda">Post-2015 Development Agenda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UN_SDGs_consulltations_in_Mariupol_(29274119644).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/UN_SDGs_consulltations_in_Mariupol_%2829274119644%29.jpg/220px-UN_SDGs_consulltations_in_Mariupol_%2829274119644%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/UN_SDGs_consulltations_in_Mariupol_%2829274119644%29.jpg/330px-UN_SDGs_consulltations_in_Mariupol_%2829274119644%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/UN_SDGs_consulltations_in_Mariupol_%2829274119644%29.jpg/440px-UN_SDGs_consulltations_in_Mariupol_%2829274119644%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UN_SDGs_consulltations_in_Mariupol_(29274119644).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UN SDG consultations in Mariupol, Ukraine</div></div></div>
<p>In 1972, governments met in Stockholm, Sweden, for the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_the_Human_Environment" title="United Nations Conference on the Human Environment">United Nations Conference on the Human Environment</a>, to consider the rights of the family to a healthy and productive environment.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In 1983, the United Nations created the <a href="/wiki/Brundtland_Commission" title="Brundtland Commission">World Commission on Environment and Development</a> (later known as the Brundtland Commission), which defined sustainable development as "meeting the needs of the present without compromising the ability of future generations to meet their own needs".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In 1992, the first <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Environment_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Conference on Environment and Development">United Nations Conference on Environment and Development</a> (UNCED) or Earth Summit was held in Rio de Janeiro, where the first agenda for Environment and Development, also known as Agenda 21, was developed and adopted.
</p><p>In 2012, the United Nations Conference on Sustainable Development (UNCSD), also known as <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Sustainable_Development" title="United Nations Conference on Sustainable Development">Rio+20</a>, was held as a 20-year follow up to UNCED. Colombia proposed the idea of the SDGs at a preparation event for Rio+20 held in Indonesia in July 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In September 2011, this idea was picked up by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Department_of_Public_Information" title="United Nations Department of Public Information">United Nations Department of Public Information</a> 64th NGO Conference in Bonn, Germany. The outcome document proposed 17 sustainable development goals and associated targets. In the run-up to Rio+20 there was much discussion about the idea of the SDGs. At the Rio+20 Conference, a resolution known as "The Future We Want" was reached by member states.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Among the key themes agreed on were poverty eradication, energy, water and sanitation, health, and human settlement.
</p><p>The Rio+20 outcome document mentioned that “at the outset, the OWG [Open Working Group] will decide on its methods of work, including developing modalities to ensure the full involvement of relevant stakeholders and expertise from civil society, the scientific community and the United Nations system in its work, in order to provide a diversity of perspectives and experience”.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2013, the 30-member UN General Assembly Open Working Group on Sustainable Development Goals was established to identify specific goals for the SDGs. The Open Working Group (OWG) was tasked with preparing a proposal on the SDGs for consideration during the 68th session of the General Assembly, September 2013 – September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> On 19 July 2014, the OWG forwarded a proposal for the SDGs to the Assembly. After 13 sessions, the OWG submitted their proposal of 17 SDGs and 169 targets to the 68th session of the General Assembly in September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> On 5 December 2014, the UN General Assembly accepted the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary General</a>'s Synthesis Report, which stated that the agenda for the post-2015 SDG process would be based on the OWG proposals.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SDG-pyramid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/SDG-pyramid.jpg/220px-SDG-pyramid.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/SDG-pyramid.jpg/330px-SDG-pyramid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/SDG-pyramid.jpg/440px-SDG-pyramid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SDG-pyramid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proposal to visualize the 17 SDGs in a thematic pyramid.</div></div></div>
<p>The annual "Le Temps Presse" festival in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> utilizes cinema to sensitize the public, especially young people, to the Sustainable Development Goals. The origin of the festival was in 2010 when eight directors produced a film titled "8," which included eight short films, each featuring one of the Millennium Development Goals. After 2.5 million viewers saw "8" on YouTube, the festival was created. It now showcases young directors whose work promotes social, environmental and human commitment. The festival now focuses on the Sustainable Development Goals.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="External_links">External links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_Development_Goals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: External links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="toccolours" style="float: right; margin: 0 0 0.8em 0.8em; width: 18.55em; border-collapse: collapse; font-size: 87%; clear: right; line-height:1.3em; background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;float:right;"><div style="float:left;"><a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Wiki_Project_Med/App" title="meta:Wiki Project Med/App"><img alt="The offline app allows you to download all of Wikipedia&#39;s medical articles in an app to access them when you have no Internet." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Tango_Phone_medapp.svg/42px-Tango_Phone_medapp.svg.png" width="42" height="47" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Tango_Phone_medapp.svg/63px-Tango_Phone_medapp.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Tango_Phone_medapp.svg/84px-Tango_Phone_medapp.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="42" data-file-height="47" /></a></div><div style="float:left;width:6px;padding:1px;height:47px;"></div>Wikipedia's health care articles can be viewed offline with the <b><a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Wiki_Project_Med/App" class="extiw" title="meta:Wiki Project Med/App">Medical Wikipedia app</a></b>.</div>
